<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Park Jae-bum" redirects here. For the golfer, see <a href="/wiki/Park_Jae-bum_(golfer)" title="Park Jae-bum (golfer)">Park Jae-bum (golfer)</a>. For the Day6 member, see <a href="/wiki/Jae_Park" title="Jae Park">Jae Park</a>.</div>

</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header">Signature</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Jayparksignature.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jayparksignature.svg/150px-Jayparksignature.svg.png" decoding="async" width="150" height="126" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jayparksignature.svg/225px-Jayparksignature.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Jayparksignature.svg/300px-Jayparksignature.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="336" /></a></span></td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Jay Park</b> (<a href="/wiki/Korean_name" title="Korean name">Korean name</a>: <b>Park Jae-beom</b> (<a href="/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">Hangul</a>: 박재범; <a href="/wiki/Hanja" title="Hanja">Hanja</a>: 朴載範); born April 25, 1987) is an American rapper, singer, songwriter, record producer, dancer and entrepreneur based in South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> He is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Breakdancing" title="Breakdancing">b-boy</a> crew <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> (AOM), and founder and former CEO of the independent <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> record labels <a href="/wiki/AOMG" title="AOMG">AOMG</a> and <a href="/wiki/H1ghr_Music" title="H1ghr Music">H1ghr Music</a>, as well as the founder of the record label More Vision.<sup id="cite_ref-jayparkofficialbio_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jayparkofficialbio-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Park returned to South Korea in June 2010 for the filming of <i>Hype Nation</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-hypenation_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hypenation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and in July, Park signed a contract with SidusHQ, one of the largest entertainment agencies in South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-sidus_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sidus-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Rebranding and re-debuting as both a solo singer and a rapper, Park's musical identity would lend to him partaking in the underground hip hop culture in South Korea, a rarity for both active and former K-Pop idols.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Known for his charismatic performances and stage presence,<sup id="cite_ref-mtv-world-stage-bieber-upstaged_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-world-stage-bieber-upstaged-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mtvasia-world-stage-bio_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvasia-world-stage-bio-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Park has been described as a "born entertainer" by Korean pop singer <a href="/wiki/Patti_Kim_(singer)" title="Patti Kim (singer)">Patti Kim</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> quoted the president of digital music distributor DFSB Kollective illustrating Park as "not just an artist, but also his own PR agent, fan club president, and TV network."<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> An influential figure in the <a href="/wiki/Korean_hip_hop" title="Korean hip hop">Korean hip hop</a> scene, Park has been described as the "scene stalwart" of Korean <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> and has been credited as one of the main figures responsible for the increased commercial acceptance and mainstream popularization of K-hip hop in South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Edmonds,_Washington" title="Edmonds, Washington">Edmonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Seattle_metropolitan_area" title="Seattle metropolitan area">Seattle metropolitan area</a>, Park showed great interest in hip hop music and breakdancing at a young age. Park attended <a href="/wiki/Edmonds_Woodway_High_School" title="Edmonds Woodway High School">Edmonds-Woodway</a>, where he spent most of his break and lunch times practicing dance with friends.<sup id="cite_ref-koreanupdates-interview_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koreanupdates-interview-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Park started listening to <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap">rap</a> music in his early teens, and spent time learning and writing raps himself during <a href="/wiki/High_school" class="mw-redirect" title="High school">high school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-imagine-tv-interview_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imagine-tv-interview-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>  In 2003, Park became one of the first members of the Seattle-based <a href="/wiki/B-boy" class="mw-redirect" title="B-boy">b-boy</a> crew <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> (AOM). Often skipping classes to participate in b-boy competitions, Park would have continuous clashes with his mother regarding his lack of interest in academics and potential higher education. In 2004, Park's mother, seeing how her son spent more time breakdancing than studying, suggested he try out for a locally advertised talent audition, which was organized by South Korean conglomerate <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> With his family financially struggling at the time, Park auditioned for the program, believing it to be a contest where the winner would receive a monetary prize reward.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Unbeknownst to Park, the success of his audition would eventually lead to him being officially contacted and selected by JYP Entertainment to be part of a Korean <a href="/wiki/Boy_band" title="Boy band">boy band</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Korean_idol" title="Korean idol">idol</a>. In January 2005, Park was brought to South Korea to receive training in dancing, rapping, singing, and the Korean language under the strict supervision of JYPE.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Park eventually completed his university education at <a href="/wiki/Dankook_University" title="Dankook University">Dankook University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2008.E2.80.932009:_2PM_and_MySpace_controversy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2008–2009:_2PM_and_MySpace_controversy">2008–2009: 2PM and MySpace controversy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2008–2009: 2PM and MySpace controversy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:2_PM_Korean_band.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2_PM_Korean_band.jpg/220px-2_PM_Korean_band.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2_PM_Korean_band.jpg/330px-2_PM_Korean_band.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/2_PM_Korean_band.jpg/440px-2_PM_Korean_band.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2566" data-file-height="1873" /></a><figcaption>2PM during a press conference for <i><a href="/wiki/Wonder_Girls" title="Wonder Girls">Wonder Girls</a> The First Wonder Live In Bangkok</i> in February 2009</figcaption></figure>
<p>Park first appeared through <a href="/wiki/Mnet_(TV_channel)" title="Mnet (TV channel)">Mnet</a>'s <i>Hot Blood Men</i>, a documentary-style reality program that showed the future members of One Day, split as idol groups <a href="/wiki/2AM_(band)" title="2AM (band)">2AM</a> and <a href="/wiki/2PM" title="2PM">2PM</a>, in training.  Park, finishing at the top spot with the most fan votes, became the leader of 2PM.<sup id="cite_ref-hotblood_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hotblood-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> On September 4, 2008, 2PM debuted with the song "<a href="/wiki/10_Out_of_10_(2PM_song)" title="10 Out of 10 (2PM song)">10 Out of 10</a>" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">10점 만점에 10점</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Ship Jeom Manjeome Ship Jeom</i>) on the music program <i><a href="/wiki/M!_Countdown" class="mw-redirect" title="M! Countdown">M! Countdown</a></i> after the release of their first mini-album, <i><a href="/wiki/10_Out_of_10_(2PM_song)" title="10 Out of 10 (2PM song)">Hottest Time of the Day</a></i>, a few days prior.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
Aside from 2PM's music activities, Park created the song "Jeong" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">정</span></span>) with <a href="/wiki/Yeeun" class="mw-redirect" title="Yeeun">Yeeun</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Wonder_Girls" title="Wonder Girls">Wonder Girls</a> for the original soundtrack of the television drama <i><a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_in_the_Court" title="Conspiracy in the Court">Conspiracy in the Court</a></i>, and featured on V.O.S's "To Luv...".<sup id="cite_ref-jeong_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jeong-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He also participated in special stage performances, such as Navi's "Heart Damage" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">마음이 다쳐서</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Maeumi Dachyeoseo</i>) on May 3, 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/K.Will" title="K.Will">K.Will</a>'s "One Drop per Second" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">1초에 한방울</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Il Choe Hanbangul</i>) on June 20, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In addition to <i><a href="/wiki/Idol_Show" title="Idol Show">Idol Show</a></i> and <i>Wild Bunny</i> with fellow 2PM members, he also became a regular cast member in several variety programs, including <i><a href="/wiki/Star_King_(TV_series)" title="Star King (TV series)">Star King</a></i> and <i>Introducing a Star's Friend</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In August 2009, he and <a href="/wiki/Kara_(South_Korean_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara (South Korean band)">Kara</a> band member, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Jung" title="Nicole Jung">Nicole Jung</a>, became the new hosts for a cultural variety show called <i>Nodaji</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 4, 2009, unfavorable comments towards Korea were found on Park's personal Myspace account from 2005. The comments, written in English to a friend, were translated by Korean media, quickly spreading across hundreds of news articles. Park expressed deep remorse and shame over his forgotten words and issued an official apology, explained the unhappiness that he experienced during his early days as a trainee in an unfamiliar country where he lacked family, the ability to easily communicate, and an understanding of the culture.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Although outraged protesters demanded that Park should be removed from 2PM, JYP Entertainment's CEO, Park Jin-young, stated on September 7, 2009, that he was going to continue as a part of the group.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The following day, Park announced on his official fancafe that he would be leaving the group to calm the situation and return to his hometown, Seattle, Washington. He also apologized to the other 2PM members, and promised that he would "come back a better person".<sup id="cite_ref-departure_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-departure-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Park Jin-young then confirmed that 2PM would continue as a six-member group.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, due to the sensitive topic of Park's departure, all 2PM members were withdrawn from their regular appearances on variety shows,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the final episode of their reality show, <i>Wild Bunny</i>, was postponed indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Park's vocals would not be removed from the older songs he promoted with 2PM, but he would be absent from the newer tracks, and the remaining six members of 2PM re-filmed their music video for "<a href="/wiki/Heartbeat_(2PM_song)" title="Heartbeat (2PM song)">Heartbeat</a>" without Park on October 31, 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>2PM's first official album was titled <i><a href="/wiki/1:59PM" class="mw-redirect" title="1:59PM">1:59PM</a></i>, to symbolize Park's absence, according to the six remaining members.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Through their acceptance speeches at end-of-year award shows for "<a href="/wiki/Again_%26_Again_(2PM_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Again &amp; Again (2PM song)">Again &amp; Again</a>", the members thanked Park and reiterated their wish for his return. At the <a href="/wiki/Mnet_Asian_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Mnet Asian Music Awards">Mnet Asian Music Awards</a>, the group paid homage to him during their performance of "Again &amp; Again" with a spotlight shown over his usual position in the dance formation and his lines left unsung.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010:_YouTube_career_and_solo_debut">2010: YouTube career and solo debut</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2010: YouTube career and solo debut">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Soon after Park returned to the United States, the South Korean public changed their perspective on the matter when they realized that his Myspace messages had been severely mistranslated and taken out of context, in addition to strong fan support for Park's return.<sup id="cite_ref-tinzarsherman_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinzarsherman-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Park was seen at <a href="/wiki/B-boy" class="mw-redirect" title="B-boy">b-boy</a> battles with fellow <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> members during his time in Seattle. However, on February 25, with Park's comeback looking more and more likely, JYP suddenly announced that Jay Park's contract with them had been terminated, citing a separate "personal mistake" that Park had made in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> JYP would make reference to this unknown event several times in 2010, but would never elaborate on any details. This termination had been agreed by all six members of 2PM and led to fan boycotts on 2PM-endorsed products. Protests for Park's return to the group began to take place, not only in South Korea, but internationally as well.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Various Jay Park-dedicated forums and fansites all over the world organized silent protests and flash dance mobs.<sup id="cite_ref-tinzarsherman_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tinzarsherman-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Fans also hired a plane with a banner showing "J, what time is it now?" to fly over Seattle, and was broadcast on Seattle-based radio stations.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On several occasions, Park was the number one trending topic on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>, even topping the <a href="/wiki/Oscars" class="mw-redirect" title="Oscars">Oscars</a> on March 8.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Park's fans revealed plans to release a self-produced album in his honor on March 27 to commemorate the 200th day anniversary of his departure from Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> However, because the album had been in preparation since January and public opinion on 2PM had since changed, the fans decided it would be in the best interest to not release the CD, and instead, mailed 10–20 copies to Seattle, Park's hometown.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park created his own YouTube channel on March 15, "jayparkaom", with the first upload being his own version of "<a href="/wiki/Nothin%27_on_You" title="Nothin&#39; on You">Nothin' on You</a>", which went viral and reached over 2,000,000 views in less than 24 hours.<sup id="cite_ref-video_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-video-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In Korea, the original song by <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Mars" title="Bruno Mars">Bruno Mars</a> topped the <a href="/wiki/Cyworld" title="Cyworld">Cyworld</a> music chart in a matter of hours upon the video's release.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> "Nothin' on You" earned $300,000 in sales through the effect of Park's video.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> On June 15, 2010, B.o.B released "Nothin' on You" featuring Park, in South Korea, where he replaces Bruno Mars' vocals. His YouTube cover helped contribute to much of the song's success in Korea, with more than 5 million copies sold.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Park subsequently thanked his fans for their support and continued to urge them not to hate remaining 2PM members.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Art_of_Movement.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Art_of_Movement.jpg/220px-Art_of_Movement.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="181" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Art_of_Movement.jpg/330px-Art_of_Movement.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Art_of_Movement.jpg/440px-Art_of_Movement.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1700" data-file-height="1400" /></a><figcaption>Park and some members of his <a href="/wiki/B-boy" class="mw-redirect" title="B-boy">b-boy</a> crew, <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>He appeared with fellow <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> members at an annual Korean-American festival event called <i>Project Korea III: KSA Cinderella Story</i> at <a href="/wiki/Rutgers_University" title="Rutgers University">Rutgers University</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>, on April 3, along with <a href="/wiki/Ailee" title="Ailee">Ailee</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clara_C" class="mw-redirect" title="Clara C">Clara C</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Videos of the event were uploaded onto internet portal sites, where footage of Park acting as an MC and dancing to <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Single_Ladies_(Put_a_Ring_on_It)" title="Single Ladies (Put a Ring on It)">Single Ladies (Put a Ring on It)</a>" on stage drew much positive interest.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On April 24, <a href="/wiki/Dumbfoundead" title="Dumbfoundead">Dumbfoundead</a> released a free collaboration track featuring Park and <a href="/wiki/Clara_Chung" title="Clara Chung">Clara Chung</a> on his website, titled "Clouds".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Los Angeles-based entertainment attorney Ned Sherman, CEO of Digital Media Wire, announced on May 28 that he was representing Park as his legal representative.<sup id="cite_ref-nedsherman_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nedsherman-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Sherman and his wife Tinzar reached out to Park, after seeing Park's story and feeling bad about what happened to him during the MySpace controversy.<sup id="cite_ref-complex_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The Shermans and Park worked on a lot of projects together, including his movie deal for <i>Hype Nation</i>, an endorsement deal with dENiZEN, <a href="/wiki/Levi_Strauss_%26_Co." title="Levi Strauss &amp; Co.">Levi Strauss &amp; Co.</a>'s new brand, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park returned to Korea on June 18 at <a href="/wiki/Incheon_International_Airport" title="Incheon International Airport">Incheon International Airport</a>, to the biggest crowd ever seen at the airport, for the filming of <i>Hype Nation</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-hypenation_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hypenation-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> "Park Jaebeom has returned" became the biggest headline in Korea that day, and "JayIsBack" shot up immediately on the trending topics on Twitter on June 18 at 9:30 AM GMT.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Pictures of Park in <i>Hype Nation</i> were released on July 2,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and Park was able to meet with the Korean media for interviews for the first time, talking about his current activities.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> It was also revealed that his single "<a href="/wiki/Demon_(Jay_Park_song)" title="Demon (Jay Park song)">Demon</a>" would be included in <i>Hype Nation'</i>s original soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was reported on July 8 that Park would sign a contract with <a href="/wiki/SidusHQ" class="mw-redirect" title="SidusHQ">SidusHQ</a> for his domestic Korean activities in terms of acting and singing;<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> his management stated that he planned to redebut as a rookie artist,<sup id="cite_ref-sidus_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sidus-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> and the contract with SidusHQ was finalized on July 16.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Park released an EP titled <i><a href="/wiki/Count_on_Me_(EP)" class="mw-redirect" title="Count on Me (EP)">Count on Me</a></i> (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">믿어줄래</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Mideojullae</i>) containing three tracks, including a rearranged Korean version of "Nothin' on You", on July 13.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The English and Korean lyrics were written by Park himself.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The EP sold 21,989 physical copies on the first day of release, coming in at number one in sales and number seven in the overall ranking of albums released from January to July 13. Without any promotion on music shows, more than 41,316 copies sold, and the EP placed at number 32 on Gaon's year end chart,<sup id="cite_ref-gaonchart.co.kr_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gaonchart.co.kr-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> earning Park approximately 700 million.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park began working with singer, producer, and fellow <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">AOM</a> member, <a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Malone" title="Cha Cha Malone">Cha Cha Malone</a>, releasing "<a href="/wiki/Bestie_(Jay_Park_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bestie (Jay Park song)">Bestie</a>" in both Korean and English, and a duet titled "<a href="/wiki/Speechless_(Jay_Park_%26_Cha_Cha_Malone_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Speechless (Jay Park &amp; Cha Cha Malone song)">Speechless</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-cha-cha-soundcloud_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cha-cha-soundcloud-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2010, Park began collaborations and forming close ties with rappers <a href="/wiki/Dok2" title="Dok2">Dok2</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Quiett" title="The Quiett">The Quiett</a> of <a href="/wiki/Illionaire_Records" title="Illionaire Records">Illionaire Records</a>, titling the partnership "AOM &amp; 1llionaire".
On September 5, Park participated in the 3rd <a href="/wiki/Wong_Fu_Productions" title="Wong Fu Productions">International Secret Agents</a> <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> concert held in Cerritos, California, together with well-known YouTube celebrities such as <a href="/wiki/Nigahiga" class="mw-redirect" title="Nigahiga">Ryan Higa</a>, <a href="/wiki/KevJumba" title="KevJumba">KevJumba</a>, <a href="/wiki/AJ_Rafael" title="AJ Rafael">AJ Rafael</a>, Alyssa Bernal, <a href="/wiki/Far_East_Movement" title="Far East Movement">Far East Movement</a>, and <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Best_Dance_Crew" title="America&#39;s Best Dance Crew">America's Best Dance Crew</a> Season 5 champions, <a href="/wiki/Poreotix" class="mw-redirect" title="Poreotix">Poreotix</a>. Park's performance drew many positive responses.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park was cast for the 2011 Korean movie <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Idol" title="Mr. Idol">Mr. Idol</a></i>, starring alongside friend and fellow <a href="/wiki/SidusHQ" class="mw-redirect" title="SidusHQ">SidusHQ</a> actor, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Su-ro" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Su-ro">Kim Su-ro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mridol_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mridol-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Park was also one of the performers, alongside <a href="/wiki/Seven_(South_Korean_singer)" title="Seven (South Korean singer)">SE7EN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taeyang" title="Taeyang">Taeyang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Musiq_Soulchild" title="Musiq Soulchild">Musiq Soulchild</a>, at the Seoul Soul Festival held at the War Memorial of Korea on October 10. Park and Musiq Soulchild also performed the latter's song "<a href="/wiki/Love_(Musiq_Soulchild_song)" title="Love (Musiq Soulchild song)">Love</a>" at the festival.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Park held a charity concert in December called the "White Love Party Concert", with <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Team_(band)" title="Supreme Team (band)">Supreme Team</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dok2" title="Dok2">Dok2</a> making appearances.<sup id="cite_ref-white-love-party-concert_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-white-love-party-concert-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Park and <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> performed at "Fever Seoul Live" alongside <a href="/wiki/Dumbfoundead" title="Dumbfoundead">Dumbfoundead</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Choi" title="David Choi">David Choi</a>, and several international b-boys.<sup id="cite_ref-fever-seoul_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fever-seoul-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In December, Park was named as <a href="/wiki/Naver" title="Naver">Naver</a>'s most searched solo singer of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2011:_Take_a_Deeper_Look_and_rise_as_a_solo_artist">2011: <i>Take a Deeper Look</i> and rise as a solo artist</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2011: Take a Deeper Look and rise as a solo artist">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On January 6, Park was announced as the winner in "Best Web Video" Category around the globe for his song "Nothin' on You" at the <a href="/wiki/Mashable_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Mashable Awards">Mashable Awards</a>, and was also nominated in the "Must Follow Personality" category, finishing second.<sup id="cite_ref-mashableaward_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mashableaward-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> At the beginning of February, Park was featured in two music videos of girl group, <a href="/wiki/5dolls" class="mw-redirect" title="5dolls">5dolls</a>, called "Lips Stains" and "It's You". Park was chosen to be the sole opener for <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a> in his first concert in Seoul for the "2011 Hyundai Mall 40th Anniversary Concert" held on March 29. He also cooperated with Ne-Yo for a charity event for children dreaming to become musicians on March 28 at the Dream Academy in Seoul.<sup id="cite_ref-neyo_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neyo-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> On March 28, Park was a finalist and received the most votes in the special category "Connecting People Award", a joint venture between <a href="/wiki/Shorty_Awards" title="Shorty Awards">Shorty Awards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nokia" title="Nokia">Nokia</a>. Park also was a finalist in the "Celebrity" category at the same event.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park released his first Korean mini-album, <i><a href="/wiki/Take_a_Deeper_Look" title="Take a Deeper Look">Take a Deeper Look</a></i>, in April, with the lead single "<a href="/wiki/Abandoned_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Abandoned (song)">Abandoned</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <i>Take a Deeper Look</i> debuted at number three in the <i>Billboard</i> World Album Charts and ranked number 26 on the Billboard Heatseekers Albums Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Park also made his debut as a solo artist on Korean music shows such as <a href="/wiki/Korean_Broadcasting_System" title="Korean Broadcasting System">KBS</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Bank_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Music Bank (TV series)">Music Bank</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Mnet_(TV_channel)" title="Mnet (TV channel)">Mnet</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/M!_Countdown" class="mw-redirect" title="M! Countdown">M! Countdown</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Munhwa_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Munhwa Broadcasting Corporation">MBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Core" class="mw-redirect" title="Music Core">Music Core</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Inkigayo" title="Inkigayo">Inkigayo</a></i>, returning for the first time in two years. Park made history as the first artist crowned winner at a debut stage, as he won <i>Music Bank</i> on May 6 and won again a week later on May 13.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 6, Park participated in his first KBS <i>Immortal Songs 2</i> episode, performing "Candy" by Korean boy band <a href="/wiki/H.O.T." title="H.O.T.">H.O.T.</a> with its leader <a href="/wiki/Moon_Hee-joon" title="Moon Hee-joon">Moon Hee-joon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Park followed up with his own R&amp;B rendition of "Aemo" by Kim Soo-hee on the next episode, which was well received.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> On his third episode of <i>Immortal Songs 2</i>, Park performed "Tell me the Truth" by <a href="/wiki/Jinusean" title="Jinusean">Jinusean</a> with <a href="/wiki/Solbi" title="Solbi">Solbi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jang_Hyuk" title="Jang Hyuk">Jang Hyuk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Su-ro" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Su-ro">Kim Su-ro</a>, and was the victor for that episode, allowing him to choose the order for the next episode.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> For his fourth episode, Park again made his own R&amp;B version of "Feel Good Day" by <a href="/wiki/Kim_Wan-sun" title="Kim Wan-sun">Kim Wan-sun</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> On his fifth episode, Park performed a remixed version of "Look Back at Me" by <a href="/wiki/Deux_(band)" title="Deux (band)">Deux</a> with a b-boy dance break.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On his sixth episode and final appearance on the show, he performed "Dear, Do Not Change" by Nam Jin and won the trophy for his last performance,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> before leaving the show to focus on his next album's preparations.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It was revealed that Park would return to <i>Immortal Songs 2</i> for a special episode "King of Kings" with other singers that have claimed the number one spot. This special episode was recorded on November 7 at the KBS Open Hall and aired on November 19.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The single "<a href="/wiki/Demon_(Jay_Park_song)" title="Demon (Jay Park song)">Demon</a>" was released on September 5 through various Korean digital music websites.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The music video was also released on the same day, and Park apologized for its low quality, saying he had no control over the release of both the music video and the song.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> "Demon" peaked at number 14 on the Gaon Chart<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> and at number 8 on the iTunes R&amp;B/Soul Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg/220px-KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="287" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg/330px-KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg/440px-KoreAm_2012-01_Cover.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="774" /></a><figcaption>Park on the cover of <a href="/wiki/KoreAm" title="KoreAm">KoreAm</a> for January 2012</figcaption></figure>
<p>Park returned to the US on October 1 to perform at the International Secret Agents Los Angeles concert.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> On October 29, Park delivered a performance to over 25,000 fans as he headlined the <a href="/wiki/MTV_EXIT" title="MTV EXIT">MTV EXIT</a> (End Exploitation and Trafficking) Live in Manila Concert held at the SM Mall of Asia. The concert also featured Californian alternative rock band, Evaline, and international singer-songwriter, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Mraz" title="Jason Mraz">Jason Mraz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park released his single "<a href="/wiki/Girlfriend_(Jay_Park_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Girlfriend (Jay Park song)">Girlfriend</a>", along with the music video via his YouTube channel on November 3.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Park performed his single on the same day at the 2011 Style Icon Awards, following a recording of tvN's Taxi.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The movie <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Idol" title="Mr. Idol">Mr. Idol</a></i> in which Park starred in was also released on November 3.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The single peaked at number 28 on the Gaon chart.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Park released Part 1 of his first full-length Korean album, <i><a href="/wiki/New_Breed_(Jay_Park_album)" title="New Breed (Jay Park album)">New Breed</a></i>, with the lead single "Star" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">별</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Byeol</i>) on December 28.<sup id="cite_ref-star_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-star-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> "Star" peaked at number one on various sites like Bugs, Olleh Music, and Soribada while being on the top of other charts of music sites.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> The first part of <i>New Breed</i> also reached the top of charts of various music sites including Olleh Music, Bugs, Soribada and Daum.<sup id="cite_ref-star_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-star-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> "Star" peaked at number 17 on the Gaon Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012:_New_Breed_and_Fresh_Air:_Breathe_It">2012: <i>New Breed</i> and <i>Fresh Air: Breathe It</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012: New Breed and Fresh Air: Breathe It">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Park received the Disk Bonsang for his mini album <i>Take a Deeper Look</i> on January 11, on the first day of the 26th <a href="/wiki/Golden_Disk_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Disk Awards">Golden Disk Awards</a>, which was held in Osaka. He was the only solo artist to receive the Disk Bonsang among the other Bonsang winners.<sup id="cite_ref-gda_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gda-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> On January 18, he received the Popular Artist Award of the Asia Model Awards, which was held in Seoul.<sup id="cite_ref-AMFA_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AMFA-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asiamodelawards1_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asiamodelawards1-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-asiamodelawards2_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asiamodelawards2-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several songs composed and written by Park for other artists were released in 2012. Jay Park produced and composed a song with <a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Malone" title="Cha Cha Malone">Cha Cha Malone</a> for Korean-American singer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Joo" title="Brian Joo">Brian Joo</a>, titled "Can't Stop".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mnet1_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnet1-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mnet2_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnet2-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Park wrote the Korean version of the song, while Joo wrote the English Version.<sup id="cite_ref-mnet1_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnet1-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mnet2_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnet2-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Park co-wrote the song "4U" for the idol group <a href="/wiki/U-Kiss" class="mw-redirect" title="U-Kiss">U-Kiss</a> at the request of main vocalist Soohyun, a long-time friend and fellow former <a href="/wiki/JYP_Entertainment" title="JYP Entertainment">JYP Entertainment</a> trainee, and it was included in U-Kiss's sixth EP <i><a href="/wiki/DoraDora" title="DoraDora">DoraDora</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-doradora-4u_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doradora-4u-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Park also produced and composed a song for the girl group <a href="/wiki/Tiny-G" title="Tiny-G">Tiny-G</a>, entitled "Polaris"; the lyrics were written by actress <a href="/wiki/Lee_Si-young" title="Lee Si-young">Lee Si-young</a>. They worked together through MBC's <i>Music and Lyrics</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> On July 3, Korean pop singer <a href="/wiki/Younha" title="Younha">Younha</a> released her fourth Korean album, <i><a href="/wiki/Supersonic_(Younha_album)" title="Supersonic (Younha album)">Supersonic</a></i>, including the track "Driver" written by Park. He also featured in the song, providing rap verses.<sup id="cite_ref-younha_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-younha-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He released his first full-length Korean album, <i><a href="/wiki/New_Breed_(Jay_Park_album)" title="New Breed (Jay Park album)">New Breed</a></i>, in February, with the lead single "Know Your Name".<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> The album reached number 1 twice on the Gaon Weekly album chart in South Korea,<sup id="cite_ref-week1_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-week1-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-week2_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-week2-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and also reached number 1 on the Hanteo Weekly chart by selling more than 80,000 copies offline in 10 days.<sup id="cite_ref-hanteo_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanteo-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hanteo2_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hanteo2-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <i>New Breed</i> debuted at number 4 on the <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i> World Album Charts and ranked number 16 on the <i>Billboard</i> Heatseekers Albums Chart.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Park made his comeback stage on Korean music shows on February 16. He won <i><a href="/wiki/Music_Bank_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Music Bank (TV series)">Music Bank</a></i> on February 24, one week after his comeback.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> On April 27, Park began Asian promotions for the Asian version release of his album <i>New Breed</i>, and visited 5 countries: <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">the Philippines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and Japan. On April 28, Jay performed at the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Star_Awards_2012" title="Star Awards 2012">Star Awards</a> in Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-asianpromotions_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asianpromotions-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> On June 13, he released the Japan editions of his albums <i>Take a Deeper Look</i> and <i>New Breed</i> through <a href="/wiki/Universal_J" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal J">Universal J</a>. The regular edition of <i>New Breed</i> includes the English version of "I Love You" and the acoustic version of "Know Your Name" as bonus tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Jay Park held his first solo concert, <i>New Breed Live in Seoul</i>, on March 3 at the Olympic Hall of <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Park,_Seoul" title="Olympic Park, Seoul">Seoul Olympic Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Park successfully held a second concert <i>New Breed Asia Tour in Seoul</i> in Seoul on August 18 at the Olympic Hall of Seoul Olympic Park.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> Park was selected as the 2012 <a href="/wiki/R-16_Korea" title="R-16 Korea">R-16 Korea</a> ambassador by the <a href="/wiki/Korea_Tourism_Organization" title="Korea Tourism Organization">Korea Tourism Organization</a> on April 23.<sup id="cite_ref-asianpromotions_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asianpromotions-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He headlined the <a href="/wiki/APAHM" class="mw-redirect" title="APAHM">APAHM</a> tour organized by <a href="/wiki/Verizon" class="mw-redirect" title="Verizon">Verizon</a> in the US in May, including concerts in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On May 16, Park released his first <a href="/wiki/Mixtape" title="Mixtape">mixtape</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Fresh_Air:_Breathe_It" title="Fresh Air: Breathe It">Fresh Air: Breathe It</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> containing songs he performed for the tour.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The mixtape was certified Gold by Datpiff within a month since its release, meaning it was downloaded over 100,000 times. Jay Park became the first artist of Asian origin to achieve this result on Datpiff.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park was the closing act at the <a href="/wiki/MTV_World_Stage_Live_in_Malaysia" title="MTV World Stage Live in Malaysia">MTV World Stage Live in Malaysia</a>, along with Canadian pop singer <a href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>, Korean girl band <a href="/wiki/Kara_(South_Korean_band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kara (South Korean band)">Kara</a>, and Malaysian singer <a href="/wiki/Mizz_Nina" title="Mizz Nina">Mizz Nina</a>, on July 14. Park also performed his song "Carefree",<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> which was included on the <i>New Breed Red Edition</i> repackaged album, and also showed his self-choreographed dance break to "<a href="/wiki/Dirty_Bass_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dirty Bass (song)">Dirty Bass</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Far_East_Movement" title="Far East Movement">Far East Movement</a> featuring <a href="/wiki/Tyga" title="Tyga">Tyga</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-mtv-world-stage-bieber-upstaged_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtv-world-stage-bieber-upstaged-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> which he later shared on YouTube.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> Park also held his own concerts in Sydney and Melbourne at the end of September 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Also in July, Park started a <a href="/wiki/Web_series" title="Web series">web series</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jay_Park_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Jay Park TV">Jay Park TV</a></i>, through his YouTube channel, filmed and edited by Hep, Park's friend and fellow <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> member.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> The web series shows Park's daily life with his friends, behind-the-scenes of concerts and filming, and the fun and games that he gets up to.
</p><p>In August, Jay Park released a music video for "New Breed", from the album of the same name, which was recorded during the album's photo shoot with Park featuring <a href="/wiki/Rick_Genest" title="Rick Genest">Rick Genest</a>-inspired make-up.<sup id="cite_ref-newbreed-mv_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newbreed-mv-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Park also uploaded a practice video to "I Love You", showing the complex choreography that he and Prepix members were practising for his upcoming concert.<sup id="cite_ref-iloveyou-practice_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iloveyou-practice-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> On August 22, Park was announced to be a fixed panel member on MBC's <i>Come to Play</i>, along with Kim Eung-soo and <a href="/wiki/Kwon_Oh-joong" title="Kwon Oh-joong">Kwon Oh-joong</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> He joined as a part of a new corner on the show, titled the "Trueman Show".<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> MBC suddenly axed the show after several months, with no prior warning to the cast nor producers.
</p><p>Later in September, Park performed for the first time in Australia, successfully holding concerts in <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-meld-magazine_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meld-magazine-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Park returned to <i>Immortal Songs 2</i> for a "King of Kings" special in October, where he performed "The Woman in Rain" by <a href="/wiki/Shin_Jung-hyeon" class="mw-redirect" title="Shin Jung-hyeon">Shin Jung-hyeon</a>. In a flying visit to <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, Jay Park made a last-minute appearance in a YouTube sketch by <a href="/wiki/David_So" title="David So">David So</a>, which parodies <a href="/wiki/Wong_Fu_Productions" title="Wong Fu Productions">Wong Fu Productions</a>' <i>The Last</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-the-last-resort_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-the-last-resort-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November, he featured on "If You Love Me", a digital single by <a href="/wiki/NS_Yoon-G" class="mw-redirect" title="NS Yoon-G">NS Yoon-G</a>. Although Park does not make an appearance in the official music video, he performed on stage with Yoon-G on music shows, with the first being <a href="/wiki/Mnet_(TV_channel)" title="Mnet (TV channel)">Mnet</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/M!_Countdown" class="mw-redirect" title="M! Countdown">M! Countdown</a></i>, and also makes an appearance in the behind-the-scenes music video, showing NS Yoon-G and Park in the studio recording the song.<sup id="cite_ref-mnet-if-you-love-me_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mnet-if-you-love-me-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> A practice video of the choreography was released soon after.<sup id="cite_ref-if-you-love-me-practice_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-if-you-love-me-practice-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
Park was the host of the December 1 episode of <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_Korea" title="Saturday Night Live Korea">Saturday Night Live Korea</a>, garnering attention for his R-rated skits, acting, and a parody music video of <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>", bringing in the highest ratings of the season for the show.<sup id="cite_ref-snl-mnet_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl-mnet-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2013:_SNL_Korea.2C_Expansion_in_Asia.2C_and_founding_of_hip_hop_label_AOMG"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2013:_SNL_Korea,_Expansion_in_Asia,_and_founding_of_hip_hop_label_AOMG">2013: <i>SNL Korea</i>, Expansion in Asia, and founding of hip hop label AOMG</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013: SNL Korea, Expansion in Asia, and founding of hip hop label AOMG">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg/220px-Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg/330px-Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg/440px-Jay_Park_at_Korean_Music_Awards_in_2013-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a><figcaption>Park accepting the award for Musician of the Year at the <a href="/wiki/Korean_Music_Awards" title="Korean Music Awards">Korean Music Awards</a>, 2013</figcaption></figure>
<p>On February 6, 2013, it was announced that Jay Park would be joining the cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live_Korea" title="Saturday Night Live Korea">Saturday Night Live Korea</a></i>, having previously hosted an episode in late 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-snl-korea-2013-announcement_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl-korea-2013-announcement-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Valentine%27s_Day" title="Valentine&#39;s Day">Valentine's Day</a>, February 14, Park released the song "Appetizer" alongside a music video. The track was  produced by friend and fellow <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> member, <a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Malone" title="Cha Cha Malone">Cha Cha Malone</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-appetizer-mnet_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-appetizer-mnet-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> On the first episode of <i>Saturday Night Live Korea</i>, Park garnered attention for his skit parodying the film <i><a href="https://ko.wikipedia.org/wiki/%ED%99%80%EB%A6%AC%EB%8D%B0%EC%9D%B4" class="extiw" title="ko:홀리데이">Holiday</a></i> with Korean actor and host of the episode, <a href="/wiki/Choi_Min-soo" title="Choi Min-soo">Choi Min-soo</a>, and for his <a href="/wiki/Ad_lib" class="mw-redirect" title="Ad lib">ad lib</a> during a skit with <a href="/wiki/Shin_Dong-yup_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Shin Dong-yup (entertainer)">Shin Dong-yup</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kim_Seul-gi" title="Kim Seul-gi">Kim Seul-gi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-snl-first-ep-choi-min-soo_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl-first-ep-choi-min-soo-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-snl-adlib-first-ep_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl-adlib-first-ep-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> on February 25, <a href="/wiki/Mizz_Nina" title="Mizz Nina">Mizz Nina</a>'s single "Around the World" featuring Jay Park was officially released. The song had been in the works since Park and Mizz Nina had performed at <a href="/wiki/MTV_World_Stage_Live_in_Malaysia" title="MTV World Stage Live in Malaysia">MTV World Stage Live in Malaysia 2012</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mtvasia-around-the-world_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mtvasia-around-the-world-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-itunes-around-the-world_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itunes-around-the-world-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> On February 28, Park received the "Musician of the Year" award at the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Korean_Music_Awards" title="Korean Music Awards">Korean Music Awards</a>, and his album <i><a href="/wiki/New_Breed_(Jay_Park_album)" title="New Breed (Jay Park album)">New Breed</a></i> was nominated in the "Best R&amp;B and Soul album" category.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-kma-award-received_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kma-award-received-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Park featured on the cover of the March edition of <i><a href="/wiki/Men%27s_Health_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Men&#39;s Health (magazine)">Men's Health Korea</a></i> magazine, and the cover was subsequently chosen by staff as the best in the magazine's 7-year history.<sup id="cite_ref-mens-health-tweet_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mens-health-tweet-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> On March 28, it was revealed that Park would be rejoining the cast of KBS' <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Freedom#Immortal_Songs_2" title="Saturday Freedom">Immortal Songs 2</a></i> for a third time.<sup id="cite_ref-rejoining-is2-april-2013_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rejoining-is2-april-2013-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following on from the success of the Jay Park's March edition of <i>Men's Health Korea</i>, the same cover was used for the April edition of <i>Men's Health China</i>, which was also the magazine's 10th anniversary edition, and included large promotional posters across the country.<sup id="cite_ref-mens-health-china-1_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mens-health-china-1-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mens-health-china-10-year_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mens-health-china-10-year-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Ustream" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustream">Ustream Korea</a>, Park held an official livestreamed event titled "Fan &amp; Music Live" on April 2,<sup id="cite_ref-ustream-event-2013_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ustream-event-2013-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> and revealed the titles of the 3 songs from his upcoming single release; "<a href="/wiki/Joah_(song)" title="Joah (song)">Joah</a>" (<a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>: <span lang="ko">좋아</span>; <a href="/wiki/Revised_Romanization_of_Korean" title="Revised Romanization of Korean">Revised Romanization</a>: <i>Joha</i>), "1 Hunnit" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">사실이야</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Sasiriya</i>), and "Welcome". The title track, "Joah", was revealed to be a mellow feel-good song, and was produced by Cha Cha Malone, with instrumentals provided by <i>Saturday Night Live Korea</i> in-session band Common Ground, "1 Hunnit" was a  rap track featuring <a href="/wiki/Dok2" title="Dok2">Dok2</a>, and "Welcome" was provocative <a href="/wiki/R%26B" class="mw-redirect" title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> track.<sup id="cite_ref-ustream-revealed-info_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ustream-revealed-info-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> On April 10, Park released the single album "Joah", along with the music video for the title track.<sup id="cite_ref-joah-enewsmnet_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joah-enewsmnet-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> The music video was filmed in Park's hometown of <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, and starred Korean actress <a href="/wiki/Clara_Lee" title="Clara Lee">Clara Lee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-joah-enewsmnet_161-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-joah-enewsmnet-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> On April 16, Park appeared on <a href="/wiki/Seoul_Broadcasting_System" title="Seoul Broadcasting System">SBS</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Hwasin_%E2%80%93_Controller_of_the_Heart" class="mw-redirect" title="Hwasin – Controller of the Heart">Hwasin – Controller of the Heart</a></i>, the sequel of <i><a href="/wiki/Strong_Heart_(TV_series)" title="Strong Heart (TV series)">Strong Heart</a></i>. On Park's 26th birthday, April 25, Park released a music video for the song "Welcome". On the April 27 episode of <i>Immortal Songs 2</i>, Park performed <a href="https://ko.wikipedia.org/wiki/%EC%9D%B4%EB%AC%B8%EC%84%B8" class="extiw" title="ko:이문세">Lee Moon-sae</a>'s "Sunset Glow" with R&amp;B singer and friend <a href="/wiki/Crush_(singer)" title="Crush (singer)">Crush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-is2-27-april_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-is2-27-april-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> Park's skit on the April 27 episode of <i>Saturday Night Live</i> with <a href="/wiki/Gayoon" class="mw-redirect" title="Gayoon">Gayoon</a> of <a href="/wiki/4Minute" title="4Minute">4Minute</a> gained attention for Park's character mistakenly saying inappropriate and sexual words in Korean, and featured a return of Park's in-character ad lib as the camera's failed to cut away at the end of the skit.<sup id="cite_ref-snl-4minute-adlib_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-snl-4minute-adlib-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On May 3, it was revealed that Park would be participating on the <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack" title="Soundtrack">soundtrack</a> of <a href="/wiki/M._Night_Shyamalan" title="M. Night Shyamalan">M. Night Shyamalan</a>'s 2013 American <a href="/wiki/Science-fiction_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Science-fiction film">science-fiction</a> <a href="/wiki/Thriller_(genre)" title="Thriller (genre)">thriller</a> film, <i><a href="/wiki/After_Earth" title="After Earth">After Earth</a></i>, having been personally contacted by <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaden_Smith" title="Jaden Smith">Jaden Smith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-after-earth-enewsworld_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-after-earth-enewsworld-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Produced by Cha Cha Malone, the song "I Like 2 Party" was the ending theme for the Korean version of the film and was written and composed by Park himself.<sup id="cite_ref-after-earth-korea-com_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-after-earth-korea-com-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-after-earth-cha-cha-i-like-to-party_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-after-earth-cha-cha-i-like-to-party-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> On May 7, Park attended the <i>After Earth</i> red carpet premiere in Korea alongside Will and Jaden Smith.<sup id="cite_ref-koream-after-earth_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-koream-after-earth-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> On May 11, <i>Immortal Songs 2'</i>s 100th episode, Park performed "Everyday Day With You" by Deulgukhwa, remixed with Park's latest single at the time, "Joah".<sup id="cite_ref-is2-every-day-with-you_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-is2-every-day-with-you-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Later that month on May 30, a song titled "Rude Girl" by Kim Seul-gi and Jay Park for was released for <a href="/wiki/Korean_drama" title="Korean drama">Korean drama</a> <i>She is Wow</i>.
</p><p>In early July, Jay Park renewed his contract with <a href="/wiki/SidusHQ" class="mw-redirect" title="SidusHQ">SidusHQ</a> after much public speculation of him signing with other record labels. He was to perform at the <a href="/wiki/Hennessy" title="Hennessy">Hennessy</a> Artistry event early in July in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>, China, alongside <a href="/wiki/B.o.B" title="B.o.B">B.o.B</a>, but the event was cancelled at the last moment due to technical difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-guangzhou-event-cancelled_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guangzhou-event-cancelled-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> On July 10, Park released a four-track <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a>, <i>I Like 2 Party</i>, alongside the music video for the title track, which was filmed in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>. On November 30, Park served as the emcee for the <a href="/wiki/BC_One" class="mw-redirect" title="BC One">Red Bull BC One</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932017:_Evolution.2C_Worldwide_and_Everything_You_Wanted"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–2017:_Evolution,_Worldwide_and_Everything_You_Wanted">2014–2017: <i>Evolution</i>, <i>Worldwide</i> and <i>Everything You Wanted</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014–2017: Evolution, Worldwide and Everything You Wanted">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On September 1, 2014, Jay Park released his second full-length album, <i>Evolution</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> With features and production from many of his <a href="/wiki/AOMG" title="AOMG">AOMG</a> labelmates such as <a href="/wiki/Simon_Dominic" title="Simon Dominic">Simon Dominic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gray_(singer)" title="Gray (singer)">Gray</a>, the album presented tributes to <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> and R&amp;B throwback ballads in its 17 tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Jay Park participated as a judge on Mnet's rap competition program <a href="/wiki/Show_Me_the_Money_4" title="Show Me the Money 4">Show Me the Money 4</a>. During the same year, Park released an extensive list of songs including "Lotto", "All I Got Time For", "On It", "Want It", "Mommae" and "Sex Trip". Park released "My Last" featuring <a href="/wiki/Loco_(rapper)" title="Loco (rapper)">Loco</a> and Gray on July 17, 2015, alongside a music video.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> On November 5, 2015, Jay Park released his third official studio album, <i>Worldwide</i>. The album was released alongside lead single "You Know (뻔하잖아)", which featured <a href="/wiki/Okasian" title="Okasian">Okasian</a> and a music video. Directed by the production company Tiger Cave, the music video starred <a href="/wiki/4Minute" title="4Minute">4Minute</a>'s <a href="/wiki/HyunA" class="mw-redirect" title="HyunA">HyunA</a> and featured cameos from other Korean talents such as rappers <a href="/wiki/Reddy_(rapper)" title="Reddy (rapper)">Reddy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ugly_Duck_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ugly Duck (rapper)">Ugly Duck</a>, among others. The hip hop project contained a total of 18 tracks and contained some of the songs Park had previously released in the year, such as "Mommae". The album also debuted at number five on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s World Albums chart. Soon after the album's release, Park released music videos for the tracks "Bo$$", "Worldwide x Want It" and "In this B*tch x My".
</p><p>On October 20, 2016, Park released his fourth solo album <i>Everything You Wanted</i>. The bilingual project contained 19 tracks and featured R&amp;B songs in both English and Korean.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Upon release the album debuted at number three on <i>Billboard</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s World Albums chart. On October 21, 2016, <a href="/wiki/Far_East_Movement" title="Far East Movement">Far East Movement</a> released their album <i>Identity</i> including the track "SXWME", which features <a href="/wiki/MNEK" title="MNEK">MNEK</a> and Jay Park.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> On July 20, 2017, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Roc_Nation" title="Roc Nation">Roc Nation</a> had signed Park for his activities in the US, marking the first ever Asian American artist on the record label.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Later that same month, it was announced that Park would be replacing <a href="/wiki/Melanie_C" title="Melanie C">Melanie C</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vanness_Wu" title="Vanness Wu">Vanness Wu</a> as one of the judges on the second season of <i><a href="/wiki/Asia%27s_Got_Talent" title="Asia&#39;s Got Talent">Asia's Got Talent</a></i>, alongside <a href="/wiki/Anggun" title="Anggun">Anggun</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Foster" title="David Foster">David Foster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, Jay Park founded record label <a href="/wiki/H1ghr_Music" title="H1ghr Music">H1ghr Music</a> with producer <a href="/wiki/Cha_Cha_Malone" title="Cha Cha Malone">Cha Cha Malone</a>, with an aim to bring both Seattle and South Korean talent to the hip hop forefront.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Currently, the label houses American and South Korean artists such as <a href="/wiki/GroovyRoom" title="GroovyRoom">GroovyRoom</a>,  <a href="/wiki/PH-1_(rapper)" title="PH-1 (rapper)">pH-1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sik-K" title="Sik-K">Sik-K</a>, Woogie, Phe Reds, <a href="/wiki/Raz_Simone" title="Raz Simone">Raz Simone</a>, and Ted Park.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.93present:_Ask_Bout_Me.2C_The_Road_Less_Traveled.2C_This_Wasn.27t_Supposed_To_Happen_and_The_Rap_of_China"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–present:_Ask_Bout_Me,_The_Road_Less_Traveled,_This_Wasn't_Supposed_To_Happen_and_The_Rap_of_China">2018–present: <i>Ask Bout Me</i>, <i>The Road Less Traveled, This Wasn't Supposed To Happen</i> and <i>The Rap of China</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2018–present: Ask Bout Me, The Road Less Traveled, This Wasn&#039;t Supposed To Happen and The Rap of China">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In May 2018, Park released his first official single under Roc Nation, "SOJU" featuring <a href="/wiki/2_Chainz" title="2 Chainz">2 Chainz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> On July 20, 2018, Park released his debut American project, an English-language EP named <i>Ask Bout Me</i>. Along with "SOJU", the seven track EP featured several notable American rappers such as <a href="/wiki/Rich_the_Kid" title="Rich the Kid">Rich the Kid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vic_Mensa" title="Vic Mensa">Vic Mensa</a>, as well as in-house production from AOMG and H1ghr Music artists such as Cha Cha Malone and GroovyRoom.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> On June 7, 2019, Park released his fifth solo studio album, <i>The Road Less Traveled</i>. The album contained features from <a href="/wiki/Jay_Electronica" title="Jay Electronica">Jay Electronica</a> and <a href="/wiki/Higher_Brothers" title="Higher Brothers">Higher Brothers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, Jay Park released a collaborative EP with American producer <a href="/wiki/Hit-Boy" title="Hit-Boy">Hit-Boy</a>, called <i>This Wasn't Supposed to Happen</i>. Named after the surprise nature of the duo's collaboration,<i>This Wasn't Supposed to Happen</i> marked Park's second release under Roc Nation, and was preceded by their single "K-Town".<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In the month after, Park collabed with Latin artist and fellow Roc Nation signee <a href="/wiki/Mozart_La_Para" title="Mozart La Para">Mozart La Para</a> for the single "Son Malas".<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Both singles contained music videos.
</p><p>Park featured as the first-ever non-Chinese guest judge in the fourth season of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Rap_of_China" title="The Rap of China">The Rap of China</a></i>, first airing on August 14, 2020. His appearance on the TV rap competition show was met with mixed reception, drawing backlash from some Chinese audiences who resented the appearance of a non-Chinese on the show, and from Korean audiences who resented the fact that Park chose to appear on the Chinese show and not the similar South Korean TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Show_Me_the_Money_(South_Korean_TV_series)" title="Show Me the Money (South Korean TV series)">Show Me The Money</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> On December 31, 2021, Park stepped down as CEO of both AOMG and H1gher Music, but remained as adviser of both companies.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>On March 3, 2022, Park established a new label called More Vision.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In July, Park will release <i>Need To Know</i> on July 12, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, it was announced that  Park would be attending the Hip-Hop Playa Festival 2022 taking place September 17–18.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> On August 16, it was announced that Park has released a teaser image for their new song "Bite", which will be released on August 18.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> In November 2022, Park was named one of <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ Korea</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Men of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artistry">Artistry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Artistry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

style="width:208px;max-width:208px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Usherraymond_(300dpi).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Usherraymond_%28300dpi%29.jpg/100px-Usherraymond_%28300dpi%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="150" class="mw-file-element"
