class="tsingle" style="width:102px;max-width:102px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg/100px-Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg" decoding="async" width="100" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg/150px-Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg/200px-Michael_Jackson_1984.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="1158" /></a></span></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a> (<i>left</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> (<i>right</i>) are two of Park's biggest influences</div></div></div></div>
<p>Park's music takes its roots in <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, more specifically from the 90s.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> He is influenced by the work of American artists he grew up listening to, such as <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginuwine" title="Ginuwine">Ginuwine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Musiq_Soulchild" title="Musiq Soulchild">Musiq Soulchild</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake" title="Justin Timberlake">Justin Timberlake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tupac" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupac">Tupac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canibus" title="Canibus">Canibus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-complex_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-neyo_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neyo-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mj_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mj-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-chrisbrown_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chrisbrown-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Park credits Usher as his idol and as one of his biggest influences, who he started listening to in the 6th grade.<sup id="cite_ref-usher_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usher-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-entermedia_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entermedia-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> He also cites Michael Jackson as his role model, as "he is the best".<sup id="cite_ref-mj_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mj-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> He cites both Usher and Michael Jackson as singers and dancers who influence him vocally and in dance, as he attempts to mimic them, looking at their music videos.<sup id="cite_ref-entermedia_197-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entermedia-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, Park also cited Chris Brown as an inspiration, and wanted “to be a singer who can be good at both singing and rapping like [him]".<sup id="cite_ref-chrisbrown_195-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chrisbrown-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Park began listening to hip hop music when he was in second grade, after one of his cousins let him listen to <a href="/wiki/Warren_G" title="Warren G">Warren G</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Regulate_(song)" title="Regulate (song)">Regulate</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-complex_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> In general, Park stated he "doesn't really listen to music to get inspiration, I listen to music because I listen to music, but I do get inspired when I listen to music, it definitely helps".<sup id="cite_ref-singapore-press-conference-2013_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singapore-press-conference-2013-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>For his dance, Park highlights <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a>, Skill Methods, and <a href="/wiki/Massive_Monkees" title="Massive Monkees">Massive Monkees</a> as b-boy crews that influence him.<sup id="cite_ref-influence_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-influence-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dance_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dance-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> He also cites Andrew Baterina from <a href="/wiki/SoReal_Cru" title="SoReal Cru">SoReal Cru</a>; Movement Lifestyle's members Keone Madrid, Lyle Beniga, and <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Evaristo" title="Shaun Evaristo">Shaun Evaristo</a>; Ian Eastwood; and Twitch.<sup id="cite_ref-influence_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-influence-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-dance_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dance-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Park is also inspired by Taiwanese-American NBA player <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Lin" title="Jeremy Lin">Jeremy Lin</a>, saying that Lin "was off the radar and now he's playing with the best of the best. People can't hate on him even though they want to because he's so good. That's how a K-pop star has to be over in America if they want to succeed. They have to be so good in every single way that even if people hate, they can't really say anything".<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style">Musical style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Musical style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Jay Park's music is generally <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">contemporary R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, but he also incorporates <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dance_music" title="Dance music">dance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acoustic_music" title="Acoustic music">acoustic</a> into his songs.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Prior to debuting with <a href="/wiki/2PM" title="2PM">2PM</a>, Park was coached vocally by former SOLID member and renowned R&amp;B artist <a href="/wiki/Kim_Jo-han" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Jo-han">Kim Jo-han</a>, also known to be the vocal coach of many idols in the industry.<sup id="cite_ref-johan_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johan-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Kim went on to say that "[Park] has an appealing and unique voice" and "definitely stood out amongst the rest".<sup id="cite_ref-johan_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-johan-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Park began to write rap lyrics in eighth grade.<sup id="cite_ref-10asia_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Since becoming a solo artist, he has complete creative control over his music&#160;: he writes and composes his own songs, produces his albums, chooses the people he wants to work with, and participates in the mastering and mixing of his songs, something almost unheard-of for a singer in the Korean music industry.<sup id="cite_ref-complex_57-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-complex-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10asia_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sound_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sound-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> More than making hit songs, Park says he wants people to hear his style of music, to make them listen to "Jay Park-sounding" music.<sup id="cite_ref-sound_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sound-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> Being fluent in both English and Korean, Park writes songs in these two languages.<sup id="cite_ref-video_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-video-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> He admits that he is more at ease when writing songs in English than in Korean, as he started learning Korean in his late teens.<sup id="cite_ref-10asia_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Park stated that the music he currently creates is "the music that I wanted to do" prior to his departure from 2PM.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> His musical process starts by listening to a lot of beats sent by various producers, while thinking of what kind of song he wants to write, and eventually short-listing a selection of potential beats to work with.<sup id="cite_ref-10asia_206-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> Then, Park works on the melody of the song, along with ideas and lyrics. He writes the hook of the song first, and finally the verses.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> Park is inspired by everything when writing songs: "just listening to good songs, seeing a good live performance, having good conversations with people. Just everyday life".<sup id="cite_ref-urbanwire_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-urbanwire-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Some songs Park wrote are influenced by songs from other artists, for example, his song "Turn Off Your Phone" (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">전화기를 꺼놔</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>Jeonhwagireur Kkeonwa</i>) from his album <i>New Breed</i> was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Leessang" title="Leessang">Leessang</a>'s hit single "Turn Off the TV ..." (Korean: <span title="Korean-language text"><span lang="ko">TV를 껐네…</span></span>; Revised Romanization: <i>TV Reurkkeotne</i>) from their 7th album <i>Asura Balbalta</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-10asia_206-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10asia-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Endorsements">Endorsements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Endorsements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In July 2010, Park was announced to be endorsing <a href="/wiki/Levi_Strauss_%26_Co." title="Levi Strauss &amp; Co.">Levi Strauss &amp; Co.</a>'s new brand, dENiZEN. He had previously revealed on YouTube in June 2010, before coming back to Korea, that he was at a photoshoot without revealing it was for dENiZEN.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> He continued to endorse the brand until the end of 2011 with female model <a href="/wiki/Kwon_Ri-se" title="Kwon Ri-se">Kwon Ri-se</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Park and Kwon recorded a remix duet song of dENiZEN's theme song, "Manifesto".<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> In early 2012, Park was chosen by <a href="/wiki/KT_Tech" class="mw-redirect" title="KT Tech">KT Tech</a> to be the official model of Take HD, a new smartphone by the brand.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Park released the maxi-single "Take HD Special Maxi Album" on February 7, 2012, produced by KT Tech to promote the smartphone.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The maxi-single includes remixes of Park's lead single from his album <i><a href="/wiki/New_Breed_(Jay_Park_album)" title="New Breed (Jay Park album)">New Breed</a></i>, "Know Your Name", released on the same day.
</p><p>Park appears with fellow SidusHQ celebrities <a href="/wiki/Jang_Hyuk" title="Jang Hyuk">Jang Hyuk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kim_Su-ro" class="mw-redirect" title="Kim Su-ro">Kim Su-ro</a>, Kim Shin-young and Jang Hee-jin in the <a href="/wiki/MMORPG" class="mw-redirect" title="MMORPG">MMORPG</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Lineage_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Lineage 2">Lineage 2</a></i> as supporting characters.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> On behalf of <a href="/wiki/Naver" title="Naver">Naver</a>'s first "Fashion Collaboration" event, Park also with fashion designer 275C for creation of a joint T-shirt titled <i>Live Free</i>, representing Park's free mind and lifestyle, and displaying both the <a href="/wiki/Space_Needle" title="Space Needle">Space Needle</a> from Seattle, his hometown, and the <a href="/wiki/Namsan_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Namsan Tower">Namsan Tower</a> from <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, where he currently lives. The back of the T-shirt shows the names of his b-boy crews <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Movement" title="Art of Movement">Art of Movement</a> and Korean Assassins, and dance collaboration team, Project Prepix Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Park was also chosen to endorse and model for casual clothing brand <a href="https://ko.wikipedia.org/wiki/%EA%B5%AC%EA%B9%80%EC%8A%A4_%EC%BB%B4%ED%8D%BC%EB%8B%88" class="extiw" title="ko:구김스 컴퍼니">Googims</a> for their 2012 collections; after the announcement was made, it was stated that "the brand's home page server was down every five minutes".<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> A behind the scenes video of Park performing an impromptu dance to "<a href="/wiki/Gangnam_Style" title="Gangnam Style">Gangnam Style</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Psy_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Psy (rapper)">Psy</a> at a Googims photo shoot was uploaded to YouTube on September 2, 2012, capturing the public's attention for his unique take of the choreography.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-korea-dot-com-gangnam-style_222-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-korea-dot-com-gangnam-style-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> Park also has been selected as the new model for outdoor clothing brand, Williamsburg, participating in TV commercials and fan-signing events.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2013, Park, a long time fan of <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>, participated at a Nike event in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, titled "Nike on Air", which was streamed live online via <a href="/wiki/Ustream" class="mw-redirect" title="Ustream">Ustream</a>. Park is currently sponsored by Nike Korea, and has modeled various times for the apparel company. In 2016, Park, alongside <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Jung" title="Jessica Jung">Jessica Jung</a>, Tian Yo, Charlene, and <a href="/wiki/Pakho_Chau" title="Pakho Chau">Pakho Chau</a> modeled for Adidas's Celebration of Sportswear campaign.  In March 2016, Park modeled for <a href="/wiki/Umbro" title="Umbro">Umbro Korea</a>'s 'Reborn to Heritage' campaign; and did a photoshoot for <a href="/wiki/Police_(brand)" title="Police (brand)">Police Sunglasses</a>, which was featured in the April issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Dazed" title="Dazed">Dazed Korea</a></i> magazine.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On March 8, 2020, a police report was filed against <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ortega" title="Brian Ortega">Brian Ortega</a> for allegedly slapping Park, who is a good friend of <a href="/wiki/Ultimate_Fighting_Championship" title="Ultimate Fighting Championship">UFC</a> <a href="/wiki/Featherweight_(MMA)" title="Featherweight (MMA)">featherweight</a> fighter <a href="/wiki/Chan_Sung_Jung" class="mw-redirect" title="Chan Sung Jung">Chan Sung Jung</a> (also known as "Korean Zombie"), and serves as his translator. The slap allegedly happened while Jung went to the bathroom at <a href="/wiki/UFC_248" title="UFC 248">UFC 248</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Park is bilingual, fluent in both English and Korean, and can speak basic Mandarin.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Jay_Park&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On March 8, 2022, Park donated <a href="/wiki/South_Korean_won" title="South Korean won">₩</a>50 million to the Hope Bridge Disaster Relief Association to help the victims of the massive wildfires that started in Uljin, Gyeongbuk, and also spread to Samcheok, Gangwon.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> On August 12, 2022, Park donated ₩100 million to help those affected by the <a href="/wiki/2022_South_Korean_floods" class="mw-redirect" title="2022 South Korean floods">2022 South Korean floods</a> through the Hope Bridge Korea Disaster Relief Association.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
